{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-10-14 10:07:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-14 10:07:00","title":"Apple reveals the $99 HomePod Mini","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059907","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Today, during its iPhone hardware event, Apple unveiled the $99 HomePod Mini.</p>\n<p>The HomePod Mini is clearly a reach for a broader swath of new users. The original HomePod managed to impress audiophiles, but its high price served as a high barrier of entry to new users looking for a new smart speaker. Complicating that &#8220;smart speaker&#8221; designation is the fact that Siri was and is several years behind the intelligence of both Amazon Alexa and Google Assistant, leaving the speaker as a more compromised choice for users who might have been hoping to embrace the fully smart home ecosystem.</p>\n<p>The new device starts shipping the week of November 16. The device comes in white and space grey colors.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The HomePod Mini ditches the trashcan Mac Pro design of its bigger relative and is much more spherical in shape, still covered in a mesh fabric. It boasts the same onboard screen that allows users to summon Siri and adjust volume, while giving the device a more interesting visual look than smart devices from other companies. Also differentiating the device is Apple&#8217;s S5 chip, which the company says helps the HomePod Mini bring users its &#8220;computational audio.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Like with the original HomePod, users can arrange a stereo pair of two of the HomePod Minis and will also be able to utilize multiple HomePod devices in a home to operate a new &#8220;Intercom&#8221; experience.</p>\n<p><div id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"http://www.dronedeploy.com/\">DroneDeploy</a>, a cloud software company that uses drone footage to help industries like agriculture, oil and gas and construction get a bird&#8217;s-eye view of a site to build a 3D picture, announced a new initiative today that combines drone photos with cameras on the ground or even ground robots from a company like <a href=\"https://www.bostondynamics.com/\">Boston Dynamics</a> for what it is calling a 360 Walkthrough.</p>\n<p>Up until today&#8217;s announcement, DroneDeploy could use drone footage from any drone to get a picture of what a site looked like outside, uploading those photos and stitching them together into a 3D model that is accurate within an inch, according to DroneDeploy CEO Mike Winn.</p>\n<p>Winn says that while there is great value in getting this type of view of the outside of a job site, customers were hungry for a total picture that included inside and out, and the platform which is simply processing photos transmitted from drones could be adapted fairly easily to accommodate photos coming from cameras on other devices.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;Our customers are also looking to get data from the interiors, and they&#8217;re looking for one digital twin, one digital reconstruction of their entire site to understand what&#8217;s going on to share across their company with the safety team and with executives that this is the status of the job site today,&#8221; Winn explained.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"KVP5lbOs1h\"><p><a has been limited, making it even more important to understand the state of the site on a regular basis.</p>\n<p>&#8220;They want fewer people on those job sites, only the essential workers doing the work. So for anyone who needs information about the site, if they can get that information from a desktop or the 3D model or a kind of street view of the job site, it can really help in this COVID environment, but it also makes it much more efficient,&#8221; Winn said.</p>\n<p>He said that while companies could combine this capability with fixed cameras on the inside of a site, they don&#8217;t give the kind of coverage a ground robot could, and the Boston Dynamics robot is capable of moving around a rough job site with debris scattered around.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2059923\" of the Boston Dynamics robot as more of an end goal, he says that more likely for the immediate future you will have a human walking through the job site with a camera to capture the footage to complete the inside-outside picture for the DroneDeploy software.</p>\n<p>&#8220;All customers already want to adopt robots to collect this data, and you can imagine a Boston Dynamics robot [doing this], but that&#8217;s the end state of course. Today we&#8217;re supporting the human walk-through as well, a person with a 360 camera walking through the job site, probably doing it once a week to document the status of the job sites,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>DroneDeploy launched in 2013 and has raised more than $100 million, according to Winn. He reports his company has over 5,000 customers, with drone flight time increasing by 2.5x YoY this year as more companies adopt drones as a way to cope with COVID.</p>\n<div class=\"embed color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px;\" target=\"_blank\"> Two Screens for Teachers</a> (@twoscreensforteachers) on <time style=\" font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\" datetime=\"2020-10-12T01:22:55+00:00\">Oct 11, 2020 at 6:22pm PDT</time></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"//www.instagram.com/embed.js\"></script></div>\n<p>Walk Score co-founders Matt Lerner and Mike Mathieu put the thing together in the first place, but a bunch of Seattle-based investors and entrepreneurs came together to raise the ~$430K needed to cover the costs of covering the whole district: &#8220;a matching grant from the Mark Torrance Foundation, a collection of early Amazon, Microsoft, and Redfin employees, and venture capitalists from the Madrona Venture Group and Pioneer Square Labs,&#8221; as the organization put it.</p>\n<p>He&#8217;s hoping that the success in Seattle will activate similar communities all over the country where there are thousands more teachers in need.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Weâ€™re asking our fellow techies in the Bay Area, Los Angeles, New York, Chicago, Denver, Salt Lake City, Atlanta, Austin, Dallas, Pittsburgh and Raleigh-Durham to show teachers they matter and keep students connected across the country,&#8221; said Lerner in a press release. Naturally other cities are welcome to join in as well, but those on the list have been challenged directly.</p>\n<p>Lerner confirmed to me that Two Screens for Teachers would happily act as an intermediary, doing discounted bulk purchases of monitors (as opposed to matching individual donors with individual teachers, which was how it got started) and having regional leaders raise cash to cover the distribution to their local educators. There&#8217;s a sort of <a href=\"https://www.twoscreensforteachers.org/blog/monitors-for-all-seattle-public-school-teachers\">how-to section in this post</a> showing how to estimate the costs and find local partners.</p>\n<p>In the spirit of friendly competition, here&#8217;s hoping other cities, and the people in them looking for a way to give back tangibly in these hard times, will take up the gauntlet and get their educators this hugely helpful resource. You can learn more (or donate) at <a href=\"https://www.twoscreensforteachers.org/\">twoscreensforteachers.com</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" id=\"speakable-summary\">Apple today introduced a new feature designed for use with its HomePod speakers, including its <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-reveals-the-99-homepod-mini/\">just-introduced HomePod Mini:</a> Intercom. Similar to Alexa&#8217;s &#8220;announce&#8221; feature, Intercom will allow HomePod owners to leverage their smart speakers &#8212; and other Apple devices &#8212; to communicate with all family members at once.</p>\n<p>The feature will make the most sense for households that have already bought into the Apple ecosystem, as you&#8217;ll be able to use Intercom across iPhone, iPad, Apple Watch, Mac and even AirPods and CarPlay.</p>\n<p>For example, as Apple demoed today, a parent could announce that it was time to go via an Apple device downstairs, and reach family throughout the home, who could then respond using the Apple device nearest them.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>To use Intercom, users would say &#8220;Hey Siri, tell everyone&#8230;&#8221; followed by the message they want to send. Message receivers could then answer by saying &#8220;Hey Siri, reply&#8230;&#8221; with their response.</p>\n<p>Technically speaking, you aren&#8217;t &#8220;shouting&#8221; across all your devices. Apple says Intercom messages will play on HomePod speakers in the home and on users&#8217; AirPods, while notifications will appear on personal devices instead.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"t51vKg4Hoo\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-reveals-the-99-homepod-mini/\">Apple reveals the $99 HomePod Mini</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple reveals the $99 HomePod Mini&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-reveals-the-99-homepod-mini/embed/#?secret=t51vKg4Hoo\" data-secret=\"t51vKg4Hoo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Apple&#8217;s ability to leverage its entire ecosystem to make a feature like Intercom more useful could prove to be a competitive advantage in the smart speaker space versus market leaders Amazon and Google &#8212; rivals that already offer Intercom-like features on their smart speakers and displays.</p>\n<p>The $99 price point for the new HomePod Mini will make it more accessible to a wider audience. Consumers may also be swayed to buy from Apple because of its support for privacy when it comes to how it handles voice recordings.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/apple-iphone-event-2020\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-event-2020.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a class=\"p1\">It took a bit longer than usual (thank COVID-19 for some insurmountable manufacturing delays), but the iPhone 12 is here. And as expected, it comes bearing 5G. The latest version of Appleâ€™s smartphone also arrives in a variety of different sizes, as the company continues to adjust to changing consumer purchasing patterns around mobile devices.</p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The inclusion of next-gen wireless is, of course, the flagship feature here. Apple is far from the first company to offer 5G on a handset, but given a bit of a bottleneck in adoption given the extremely odd year we&#8217;ve been experiencing. According to recent numbers from Canalys, only 13% of handsets shipping in the first half of the year were 5G capable. That means there&#8217;s a long way to go, and Apple finally adopting the tech will certainly move the needle.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2060015\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"610\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg 1419w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg?resize=150,89 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg?resize=300,179 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg?resize=768,457 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg?resize=680,405 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-12-blue.jpg?resize=50,30 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>CEO Tim Cook kicked off the announcement by inviting Verizon (TC&#8217;s parent co.) on stage to sell the carrier&#8217;s UWB take on the tech and announce that it&#8217;s gone &#8220;nationwide.&#8221; 5G will be available on all of the new models announced today. The specifics of the 5G will vary based on location &#8212; here in the States, for example, mmwave will also be available.</p>\n<p>As expected, the line gets a full redesign, borrowing cues from the iPad Pro, including a flat edge more in line with older devices than the newer curved models. The device is also 11% thinner and lighter than its predecessor. The redesign also makes it possible for the company to pack more antennas into the edge of the device.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2060126\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"568\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg 1473w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg?resize=150,83 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg?resize=300,166 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg?resize=768,426 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg?resize=680,377 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.42.29-PM.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p>There&#8217;s a Corning glass display. Apple says it worked directly with with the Gorilla Glass maker to develop ceramic shield, which it states is around six-times more reliable in drop tests. The smartphone sports an OLED display (which appears to be consistent across the new devices, as well), with double the number of pixels as the iPhone 11.</p>\n<p>The handset sports the already-announced <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/apple-unveils-its-super-fast-five-nanometer-a14-chip-shipping-in-the-new-ipad-air-next-month/\">A14 bionic chip</a>. Apple&#8217;s silicon sports six-cores on its CPU and four on its GPU. The latter will go a ways toward extending its position in mobile gaming. The company used that opportunity to announce that it will be bringing Riot Games&#8217; League of Legends: Wild Rift to the handset. As anticipated, the base model 12 sports a dual-camera rear &#8212; with 12-megapixel wide and ultra-wide lenses. Night Mode has been improved across the devices and added to the front camera.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2060110\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"572\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg 1456w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg?resize=300,168 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg?resize=768,429 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg?resize=680,380 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.37.27-PM.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<div class=\"ncpost-list-post\" role=\"article\" aria-labelledby=\"ncpost-list-post-title-1615444\" aria-describedby=\"ncpost-list-post-content-1615444\" aria-posinset=\"14\" aria-setsize=\"184\">\n<div class=\"ncpost-container\" data-ncpost-id=\"1615444\">\n<div class=\"ncpost-header\">\n<div class=\"ncpost-timestamp\">The MagSafe name is back &#8212; albeit far removed from the version we all fondly remember from the Mac. Here it refers to a magnetic system built into the rear of the device that lets compatible accessories snap directly onto the device. That includes a slew of different products from Apple and third-parties, including wireless charging pads and cases. The list includes Apple&#8217;s own combination phone/Watch charger &#8212; not quite AirPower, but still fun.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n<div><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-2060106\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"572\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg 1456w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg?resize=300,168 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg?resize=768,429 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg?resize=680,380 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.36.37-PM.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></div>\n<div>Speaking of charging, the Lightning port is still very much on-board, in-spite of dropping it on some iPad models. accessories without worrying about the sticker on the back losing its adhesiveness over time and needing a rinse.</p>\n<p>MagSafe, Apple&#8217;s charging brand, is now the company&#8217;s new system today</a> at Apple&#8217;s iPhone event.</p>\n<p>Thanks to the new array of magnets positioned around the wireless charging coil, the iPhone will be better aligned when connected with Apple&#8217;s MagSafe Charger and MagSafe Duo Charger &#8212; designed for wirelessly charging the iPhone 12 and iPhone 12 plus Apple Watch, respectively.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/\">Apple launches new ecosystem of accessories and wireless chargers with chargers with MagSafe&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/embed/#?secret=TfCoES6ERV\" attachable iPhone wallet. The company also <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2020/10/apple-announces-iphone-12-and-iphone-12-mini-a-new-era-for-iphone-with-5g/\">said</a> on Tuesday that consumers should expect a range of MagSafe accessories from third-party manufacturers.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;ll admit, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/sarahintampa/status/1316059763755618304\">my mind was on PopSockets for some reason</a> before the Apple event. Which is why when MagSafe was introduced, my first thought was <em>oh, PopSockets!Â </em></p>\n<p>I&#8217;m probably not alone.</p>\n<p>The company has sold more than 165 million PopSockets Grips since launching in 2014, and has since expanded its grippy-things-on-the-back-of-your-phone product line to include all sorts of variations &#8212; like PopSockets with mirrors or lip gloss, tiny versions, PopSockets with wallets, Otter + PopSockets phone cases and even PopSockets that match your nails. (Oh, and they&#8217;ve got <a href=\"https://www.popsockets.com/shop/face-mask?lang=en_US\">face masks</a> to match your PopSockets now, too.)</p>\n<p>PopSockets Grips can be removed a number of times, but they can lose their stickiness over time. The company says the solution is to give the little dongle a rinse and let it air dry for about 10 minutes, then stick it back on the iPhone and let it set for a couple of hours.</p>\n<p>This can be a bit of a tedious process, which is why the company introduced PopSockets Grips with interchangeable covers, aka PopTops.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"d3De7yYrxS\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/this-is-the-iphone-12/\">Apple&#8217;s iPhone 12 starts at $799, sporting 5G and a magnetic adapter</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple&#8217;s iPhone 12 starts at $799, sporting 5G and a magnetic adapter&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/this-is-the-iphone-12/embed/#?secret=d3De7yYrxS\" data-secret=\"d3De7yYrxS\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>However, a line of MagSafe-compatible PopSockets line would mean you wouldn&#8217;t have to worry about the product&#8217;s stickiness wearing off. As a result, users might be induced to buy more of these iPhone dongles &#8212; perhaps even accumulating a collection they can swap out at will, to match their outfits or mood.</p>\n<p>It also means that users could forgo having to use a case with their iPhone &#8212; as iPhone 11 owners currently have to &#8212; in order to take advantage of PopSockets Grips.</p>\n<p>Conversely, it could open PopSockets to more competition in the accessories market, as companies won&#8217;t have to out-engineer the Grips and their <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/popsockets-successfully-defends-its-patent-against-competitor-challenge-300987315.html\">patent</a>-protected technology. Instead, rivals could simply expand their existing product lines with MagSafe-compatible items for an upcharge and increase their revenues.</p>\n<p>PopSockets says it has MagSafe products in development, but isn&#8217;t announcing details at this time.</p>\n<p><em>Note: Image does not show MagSafe-compatible products.Â </em></p>\n<p><a 10:07:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-14 10:07:00","title":"Should you replace your developer portal with a hybrid integration platform?","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059497","description":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter</title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"/>\t</svg>\n\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tPeter Kreslins is co-founder and CTO of <a href=\"https://digibee.com/\">Digibee</a>, a leader in holistic and agile approaches to systems integration.\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">The concept of a developer portal is to provide the necessary technical information to configure and manage the communication between an API and both internal and external systems. Originally, it was not thought of as a business-generating tool for companies that adopt them. Rather, it was an interface between APIs, SDKs and other digital tools and their administrators.</p>\n<p>However, over time, many developer portal elements have caused friction for partners and resulted in higher costs for the company providing the data through APIs.</p>\n<p>An alternative option to replace a developer portal is a Hybrid Integration Platform (HIP), a simple system connection solution that has the potential to generate more business through pairing ecosystems directly, efficiently and at a lower cost.</p>\n<h2>Fixing potential developer portal problems</h2>\n<p>The leading cause of friction within a developer portal is the amount of time it takes to create and support it. Quite often, an integration is delayed because the company providing the API is stuck waiting for support from the people they are working with.</p>\n<p>To fulfill the demand for consumers in different stages of maturity, companies providing APIs later realized they needed to provide more data, new business cases and different mappings and transformations.</p>\n<p>Once the portal and APIs adapt to the system, three key factors are necessary to provide a good user experience in the developer portal:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Complete and easy-to-use documentation.</li>\n<li>Actionable and effective solution options.</li>\n<li>Quick response time.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Frequently, isolated and disconnected business challenges complicate developer portal implementations. To avoid such challenges, you should address these questions before the implementation process takes place:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>How can you ensure the business will benefit from the connection with partners, suppliers and customers?</li>\n<li>Is it possible to become more efficient, have lower integration costs and improve implementation and adoption times for technological solutions?</li>\n<li>How is innovation unlocked when previously unavailable data and services are made internally available?</li>\n</ol>\n<p>When approaching a systems integration, itâ€™s essential to develop a solution that considers business results first, before simplifying or removing any technical issues. Fixing predicted issues before they become problems only wastes time and takes the focus off the goal of making your business more efficient and profitable. Yet, many times we see the opposite happen â€” businesses tend to spend too much time fixing problems before they even occur.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"tkD0XmKwfb\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/28/can-api-vendors-solve-healthcares-data-woes/\">Can API vendors solve healthcare&#8217;s data woes?</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Can API vendors solve healthcare&#8217;s data woes?&#8221; &#8212; id=\"speakable-summary\">Apple <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-unveils-its-flagship-5g-phones-the-iphone-12-pro-and-pro-max/\">introduced</a> its latest flagship iPhone models, the iPhone 12 Pro and 12 Pro Max, at its iPhone event on Tuesday. Among other things, the devices sport a new LiDAR Scanner designed to allow for more immersive augmented reality (AR) experiences. Snapchat today confirms it will be among the first to put the new technology to use in its iOS app for a lidar-powered Lens.</p>\n<p>As Apple explained during the event, the LiDAR (Light Detection And Ranging) Scanner measures how long it takes for light to reach an object and reflect back.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"fQw08He4GS\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-unveils-its-flagship-5g-phones-the-iphone-12-pro-and-pro-max/\">Apple unveils its flagship 5G phones, the iPhone 12 Pro id=\"speakable-summary\">At Apple&#8217;s iPhone event on Tuesday, the company introduced a range of new phones, led by the <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/newsroom/2020/10/apple-introduces-iphone-12-pro-and-iphone-12-pro-max-with-5g/\">just-announced</a> flagships: the iPhone 12 Pro, starting at $999, and iPhone 12 Pro Max, starting at $1099. The new 5G-ready devices sport an all-screen Super Retina XDR display, the A14 Bionic chip, a Ceramic Shield front cover, LiDAR Scanner, and of course, the iPhone line&#8217;s best camera system.</p>\n<p>iPhone 12 Pro and iPhone 12 Pro Max will be available in 128GB, 256GB, and 512GB configurations and four stainless steel finishes, including graphite, silver, gold, and pacific blue.</p>\n<p>5G, of course, will be one of the bigger selling points for the devices as the new technology will boost speeds, meaning faster downloads and uploads, higher quality streaming, more responsive gaming and faster responses in apps, among other things.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Of course, some of the immediate demand for new 5G phones may be tempered by the coronavirus pandemic, which is causing economic hardships for many &#8212; particularly in markets like the U.S. where the virus is still spinning out of control. Work-from-home users may also not feel as strong a need for an immediate upgrade to the technology, as they would have before the pandemic, given that many are now spending a larger portion of their time indoors on their home Wi-Fi.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060240\" style=\"width: 526px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060240\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060240\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?w=516\" alt=\"\" width=\"516\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg 1306w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?resize=114,150 114w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?resize=228,300 228w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?resize=768,1013 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?resize=516,680 516w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?resize=1165,1536 1165w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-stainless-steel-gold_10132020.jpg?resize=38,50 38w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 516px) 100vw, 516px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060240\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>In the U.S., Apple says the iPhone 12 Pro models will be able to reach speeds of up to 4Gbps, even in densely populated areas. A &#8220;Smart Data&#8221; feature will also help with the transition to faster speeds, by intelligently balancing data usage and battery power in real-time.</p>\n<p>Inside, the new devices also include the A14 Bionic chip, featuring a 16-core Neural Engine â€” for an 80% increase in performance, Apple claims. It&#8217;s capable of completing 11 trillion operations per second, and is faster and more efficient than prior iterations.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mCKVVR1Nkr\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/heres-everything-apple-announced-at-its-hi-speed-iphone-event-today/\">Here&#8217;s everything Apple announced at its &#8220;Hi, Speed&#8221; iPhone event today</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Here&#8217;s everything Apple announced at its &#8220;Hi, Speed&#8221; iPhone event today&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/heres-everything-apple-announced-at-its-hi-speed-iphone-event-today/embed/#?secret=mCKVVR1Nkr\" data-secret=\"mCKVVR1Nkr\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Aesthetically, the new iPhones will look somewhat different too.</p>\n<p>The 6.1-inch iPhone 12 Pro and 6.7-inch iPhone 12 Pro Max will now have a flat-edge design and an edge-to-edge OLED display with reduced borders. These &#8220;squarer&#8221; edges give the device a more classic look reminiscent of older model iPhones.</p>\n<p>On the Pro Max, iPhone gets its biggest-ever screen and the highest resolution, at neary 3.5M pixels.</p>\n<p>The back for these new devices is matte glass and the phone sports at stainless steel band, around the edges. But what&#8217;s new is something Apple is calling &#8220;Ceramic Shield.&#8221; This tougher front cover aims to improve the &#8220;shatterability,&#8221; so to speak, which Apple claims improves drop performance by 4x compared with iPhone 11 Pro. (Oh, we&#8217;ll see!)</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060239\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060239\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060239\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"382\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg 1960w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_announce-iphone12pro_10132020.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060239\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>The iPhone 12 Pro models are also water resistant for up to 6 meters for 30 minutes (or the IP68 rating, as it&#8217;s known.)</p>\n<p>Another key reason people opt for the high-end models is the camera system, of course.</p>\n<p>This time around, Apple says it&#8217;s aided by a new image signal processor (ISP), the A14 Bionic, and the models will feature &#8220;Apple ProRAW&#8221; later this year. This format combines Apple&#8217;s multiframe image processing and computational photography capabilities with the versatility of the RAW format. In practice, this means users will be able to exert creative control over color, detail and dynamic range both natively on the iPhone and using third-party photo editing tools.</p>\n<p>The iPhone 12 Pro features also a new 7-element lens Wide camera with an Æ’/1.6 aperture, the fastest now available in the iPhone line, and promising improvements in low-light video and photos. The Ultra Wide camera has a 12-degree field of view, while the Telephoto camera has a 52 mm focal length, bringing the optical zoom range to 4x.</p>\n<p>The iPhone 12 Max ups things further with a 47% larger sensor with 1.7Î¼m pixels for a 87% improvement in low-light conditions, Apple claims. It also has the Ultra Wide camera and a Telephoto camera with a 65 mm focal length, for a 5x optical zoom range.</p>\n<p>Night mode has also now been expanded the to TrueDepth and Ultra Wide cameras, and Night mode Time-Lapse promises sharper videos, better light trails, and smoother exposure when used with a tripod.</p>\n<p>Deep Fusion is also now faster, and Smart HDR 3 is an update for more true-to-life images, says Apple.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060241\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060241\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060241\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"382\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg 1960w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Apple_iphone12pro-ios14-photos-edit_10132020.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060241\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>For video, the new models offer HDR video with Dolby Vision, up to 60 fps, and improved video stabilization. Users can even share their 4K Dolby Vision videos on AirPlay.</p>\n<p>Also new is the LiDAR Scanner, which matters for AR (augmented reality).</p>\n<p>The improvement here means faster and more realistic AR with an improved autofocus by 6x in low-light scenes. That could lead to some interesting new apps and experiences within apps, like Snapchat filters. (We spotted Snapchat in the demo briefly, though it wasn&#8217;t specifically mentioned.)</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AqyvEkR9lx\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/\">Apple launches new ecosystem of accessories and wireless chargers with MagSafe</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple launches new ecosystem of accessories and wireless chargers with MagSafe&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/embed/#?secret=AqyvEkR9lx\" data-secret=\"AqyvEkR9lx\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Another consumer-friendly feature coming to the new iPhone models is MagSafe, which helps with wirelessly charging as well as allowing users to snap on magnetic accessories, like Apple&#8217;s new Leather Wallet with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/\">MagSafe</a>. These will go on sale along with the MagSafe Charger and iPhone 12 Pro Silicone Case and Clear Case on Oct. 16. Leather Cases will go on sale Nov. 6. A MagSafe Duo Charger and Leather Sleeve will later follow.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060244\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060244\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060244\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>Pre-orders for iPhone 12 Pro begin Friday, October 16 at 5 AM PDT, with availability beginning Friday, October 23. iPhone 12 Pro Max will be available for pre-order Friday, November 6 at 5 AM PST, and in stores beginning Friday, November 13.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Everyone had a pretty good feeling this would be the one where they announced this year&#8217;s new iPhone&#8230; instead, Apple announced <em>four</em> new iPhones, plus a new HomePod, for good measure.</p>\n<p>Didn&#8217;t have time to follow along live? Here are the highlights:</p>\n<h2>HomePod Mini</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060087\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060087\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2060087 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"375\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg 1430w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg?resize=150,83 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg?resize=300,165 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg?resize=768,423 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg?resize=680,375 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-13-at-1.06.57-PM.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060087\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Apple kicked things off by announcing <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-reveals-the-99-homepod-mini/\">the HomePod Mini</a> â€” which, as you&#8217;ve probably gathered from the name, is a smaller version of its HomePod speaker.</p>\n<p>Apple&#8217;s focus with the HomePod Mini definitely seems to be getting you to buy multiple units and spreading them around your house â€” they started off by recapping Siri&#8217;s smart home capabilities, then introduced <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apples-new-intercom-feature-will-let-you-shout-across-your-apple-devices/\">a new feature called &#8220;Intercom,&#8221;</a> which lets you broadcast a message to all of your HomePods from your iPhone, Apple Watch, CarPlay or another HomePod. Put two HomePods in the same room, Apple says, and they&#8217;ll automatically become a stereo pair.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"sXnKfBsYuK\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apples-new-intercom-feature-will-let-you-shout-across-your-apple-devices/\">Apple&#8217;s new &#8216;Intercom&#8217; feature will let you shout across your Apple devices</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple&#8217;s new &#8216;Intercom&#8217; feature will let you shout across your Apple devices&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apples-new-intercom-feature-will-let-you-shout-across-your-apple-devices/embed/#?secret=sXnKfBsYuK\" data-secret=\"sXnKfBsYuK\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>HomePod Mini will cost $99, and, like its bigger counterpart, will come in two colors: white and space grey. Pre-orders will start on November 6th, with the first units shipping &#8220;the week of November 16th.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>Four new iPhones</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060197\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060197\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060197\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"iPhone 12 family lineup\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg 1218w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg?resize=768,433 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12_family-lineup.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060197\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>Why would Apple announce one new iPhone when they could announce <em>four</em>?</p>\n<p>With a lineup that will probably lead to aÂ bit of confusion,<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/this-is-the-iphone-12/\"> Apple today announced the iPhone 12 Mini, iPhone 12, iPhone 12 Pro and iPhone 12 Pro Max</a>. The devices get a little bigger, a little fancier and a bit more expensive as you go down the line. <strong>Want a deeper look at how the specs on the four new models compare? Find<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apples-iphone-12-12-mini-12-pro-and-12-pro-max-whats-the-difference/\">Â our side-by-side here</a>.</strong></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PLL1XFjAqJ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apples-iphone-12-12-mini-12-pro-and-12-pro-max-whats-the-difference/\">Appleâ€™s iPhone 12, 12 mini, 12 Pro and 12 Pro Max: whatâ€™s the difference?</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Appleâ€™s iPhone 12, 12 mini, 12 Pro and 12 Pro Max: whatâ€™s the difference?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apples-iphone-12-12-mini-12-pro-and-12-pro-max-whats-the-difference/embed/#?secret=PLL1XFjAqJ\" data-secret=\"PLL1XFjAqJ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The big focus here is on improved displays, improved cameras (night mode on the wide and ultra-wide cameras!) and the introduction of 5G support across the lineup. The form factor borrows some angles from iPhones of yesteryear, with flat sides that&#8217;ll probably remind you of the iPhone 4 or 5.</p>\n<p>The iPhone 12 Mini will start at $699 and come with a 5.4&#8243; display, while the iPhone 12 will start at $799 with a 6.1&#8243; display. The iPhone 12 Pro will start at $999 with a 6.1&#8243; display, but polishes up the spec sheet with a stainless steel body (versus aluminum on the non-pro models) and the addition of a 12MP telephoto lens. The iPhone 12 Pro Max will start at $1,099, but packs a massive 6.7&#8243; display. The Pro models also pack lidar sensors, allowing them to do things like ultra-fast focusing in low-light situations, or 3D room scanning.</p>\n<p>The displays on all of the new iPhones will feature a new &#8220;Ceramic Shield&#8221; technology that Apple built in partnership with Corning, which the company says improves the odds of your device surviving a fall by 4x. The iPhone 12 and 12 Mini will come in blue, green, red, white and black; the 12 Pro and 12 Pro Max, meanwhile, will come in blue, gold, black and white.</p>\n<p>All four phones will run on Apple&#8217;s A14 Bionic chip â€” the same one that powers <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/apple-unveils-its-super-fast-five-nanometer-a14-chip-shipping-in-the-new-ipad-air-next-month/\">the iPad Air the company just announced last month</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"N4rkwgAHak\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/apple-unveils-its-super-fast-five-nanometer-a14-chip-shipping-in-the-new-ipad-air-next-month/\">Apple unveils its super fast five nanometer A14 chip, shipping in the new iPad Air next month</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple unveils its super fast five nanometer A14 chip, shipping in the new iPad Air next month&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/apple-unveils-its-super-fast-five-nanometer-a14-chip-shipping-in-the-new-ipad-air-next-month/embed/#?secret=N4rkwgAHak\" data-secret=\"N4rkwgAHak\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>So when will these things actually start shipping? The pre-order/ship dates are a<em> liiiiittle</em> bit tangled â€” so if you&#8217;ve got a model picked out already, make sure you&#8217;ve got the right date marked on your calendar: the iPhone 12 and 12 Pro go up for pre-order on 10/16, shipping on 10/23. The iPhone 12 Mini and the 12 Pro Max, meanwhile, go up for pre-order on 11/6 and ship on 11/13.</p>\n<p>(Apple also noted that it will continue to sell the iPhone 11, dropping the base price by $100 down to $599.)</p>\n<h2>MagSafe</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060206\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060206\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060206\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/iPhone-12-Pro-Silicone-Case_Leather-Wallet-with-MagSafe.gif?w=680\" alt=\"iPhone 12 Pro Silicone Case_Leather Wallet with MagSafe\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060206\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/\">&#8220;MagSafe&#8221; is back</a>! Sort of. Well, in name, at least.</p>\n<p>Borrowing a name from the charging system of Apple laptops past, the new iPhone&#8217;s MagSafe system allows it to automatically snap into the optimal place on a wireless charger, while also allowing for snap-on accessories like magnetic cases or credit card holders.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"NRoegbDrlQ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/\">Apple launches new ecosystem of accessories and wireless chargers with MagSafe</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple launches new ecosystem of accessories and wireless chargers with MagSafe&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-launches-new-ecosystem-of-accessories-and-wireless-chargers-with-magsafe/embed/#?secret=NRoegbDrlQ\" data-secret=\"NRoegbDrlQ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The company also announced the MagSafe Duo Charger (a folding setup meant to allow you to charge both an iPhone and an Apple Watch) and noted that MagSafe-compatible accessories from third parties like Belkin were on the way.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060205\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060205\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2060205\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"MagSafe Duo Charger\" width=\"680\" height=\"382\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg 1300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/MagSafe-Duo-Charger.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060205\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<h2>No more power adapter or headphones in the box</h2>\n<p>It&#8217;s been rumored for months, but now it&#8217;s official: <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/iphones-wont-come-with-headphones-or-power-adapters-in-the-box-from-now-on/\">Apple will no longer be including headphones or a wall power adapter with the iPhone</a>. The company cites the potential environmental impact as their reasoning, noting that there are already &#8220;billions&#8221; of compatible chargers out in the world. The new iPhones <em>will</em> ship with a USB-C to Lightning cable â€” just not the bit that plugs into the wall.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/apple-iphone-event-2020\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-event-2020.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=l4y0XFrXqXo:709EfDWRrxo:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a 10:07:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-14 10:07:00","title":"IPhones wonâ€™t come with headphones or power adapters in the box from now on","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2060117","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">That drawer full of bad headphones and extra power adapters for your phone won&#8217;t get any more cluttered if you decide to pick up a new iPhone 12. Apple will no longer include those items in the box, part of a redoubled effort to reduce its environmental footprint.</p>\n<p>In a segment of its iPhone-centric event today, Apple&#8217;s Lisa Jackson explained that the company is hoping to have &#8220;net zero climate impact&#8221; globally by 2030, meaning everything from manufacturing and assembly to packaging and device recycling will be carbon neutral. Achieving that means relying more on solar power and efficient operations, of course, but also reducing waste.</p>\n<p>To that end the company will no longer include the familiar white headphones that have come in the box since the early days of the iPhone, nor the standard outlet adapter for the power cable.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Customers already have over 700 million Lightning headphones, and many customers have moved to a wireless experience,&#8221; said Jackson. &#8220;There are also over 2 billion Apple power adapters out in the world, and that&#8217;s not counting the billions of third-party adapters.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FQWaSPJ6UC\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/04/18/apple-expands-global-recycling-programs-announces-new-material-recovery-lab-in-austin/\">Apple expands global recycling programs, announces new Material Recovery Lab in Austin</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple expands global recycling programs, announces new Material Recovery Lab in Austin&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/04/18/apple-expands-global-recycling-programs-announces-new-material-recovery-lab-in-austin/embed/#?secret=FQWaSPJ6UC\" data-secret=\"FQWaSPJ6UC\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Thankfully there will be a power cable in the box: a standard USB-C to Lightning cable that you can plug into your old wall adapter or a laptop. Well, not the <em>old</em> old ones, but the fairly recent ones. To be honest, you might need a dongle.</p>\n<p>The result is not just fewer things in the box, but a smaller actual box, letting the company fit more of them into a pallet. That may sound like a bit of a stretch for effect â€” &#8220;really, you&#8217;re saving the world by making the box smaller?&#8221; â€” but at the scales Apple operates at, fitting half again as many devices into a shipment means saving thousands of trips. It&#8217;s the equivalent, Apple notes, of taking some 450,000 cars off the road per year.</p>\n<p>Apple didn&#8217;t mention its part in creating an endless yearly cycle of questionably necessary replacements of perfectly good devices, or in making millions of accessories obsolete with choices like <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/12/25/i-still-miss-the-headphone-port/\">removing the headphone jack</a>, but that&#8217;s to be expected. They may be part of the problem there, but so is every other major consumer electronics manufacturer, and at least Apple is trying to balance things out a bit.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/apple-iphone-event-2020\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-event-2020.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"embed +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-event-2020.jpg","linkMd5":"b1ab3a4dab136114ec457db820c84b83","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn20@2020_2/2020/10/14/02-07-00-842_48e2fa61d2265c29.webp","destWidth":3200,"destHeight":440,"sourceBytes":169448,"destBytes":38014,"author":"Devin 10:07:00","updatedTime":"2020-10-14 10:07:00","title":"Appleâ€™s iPhone 12 Pro camera upgrades sharpen focus on serious photographers","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2060226","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/apple-iphone-event-2020\">Apple&#8217;s iPhone 12 Pro</a> heaps improvements on the already formidable power of its camera system, adding features that will be prized by &#8220;serious&#8221; photographers â€” that is to say, the type who like to really mess around with their shots after the fact. Of course, the upgrades will also be noticeable for us &#8220;fire and forget&#8221; shooters as well.</p>\n<p>The most tangible change is the redesign of two of the three lens systems on the rear camera assembly. The Pro Max comes with a new, deeper telephoto camera: a 65 mm-equivalent rather than the 52 mm found on previous phones. This closer optical zoom will be prized by many; after all, 52 mm is still quite wide for portrait shots.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2UVfljWhNX\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-unveils-its-flagship-5g-phones-the-iphone-12-pro-and-pro-max/\">Apple unveils its flagship 5G phones, the iPhone 12 Pro and Pro Max</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple unveils its flagship 5G phones, the iPhone 12 Pro and Pro Max&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/apple-unveils-its-flagship-5g-phones-the-iphone-12-pro-and-pro-max/embed/#?secret=2UVfljWhNX\" data-secret=\"2UVfljWhNX\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The improved wide-angle lens, common to all the new iPhone 12 models, has had its lens assembly simplified down to seven elements, improving light transmission and getting its equivalent aperture to F/1.6. At this scale, practically every photon counts, especially for the revamped Night Mode.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060322\" style=\"width: 1079px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060322\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2060322 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg\" alt=\"A disassembled iPhone camera.\" width=\"1069\" height=\"769\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg 1069w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg?resize=150,108 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg?resize=300,216 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg?resize=768,552 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg?resize=680,489 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/lens-elements.jpg?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1069px) 100vw, 1069px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060322\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>Perhaps a more consequential (and portentous) hardware change is the introduction of sensor-level image stabilization to the wide camera. This system, first used in DSLRs, detects motion and shifts the sensor a tiny bit to compensate for it, thousands of times per second. It&#8217;s a simpler, lighter-weight alternative to solutions that shift the lens itself.</p>\n<p>Practically every flagship phone out there has some form of image stabilization, but implementations matter, so hands-on testing will determine whether this one is, in Apple&#8217;s words, &#8220;a game changer.&#8221; At any rate, it suggests that this is going to be a feature of the iPhone camera system going forward, and gains we see from it are here to stay; the presenter at today&#8217;s virtual event suggested a full F-stop, allowing two-second handheld exposures, but I&#8217;d take that with a grain of salt.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060323\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060323\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2060323\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg\" alt=\"An image showing the layers of a picture processed by an iPhone.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"671\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg 1349w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg?resize=150,98 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg?resize=300,197 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg?resize=768,503 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg?resize=680,446 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/appleproraw.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060323\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>On the software side, the introduction of Apple ProRAW will be a godsend to photographers who use the iPhone either as a primary or secondary camera. When you take a photo, only a fraction of the information the sensor collects ends up on your screen â€” a huge amount of processing goes into removing redundant data, punching up colors, finding a good tone curve and so on. This produces a good-looking image at the cost of customizability; once you throw away that &#8220;extra&#8221; information, the colors and tone are restricted to a much narrower range of adjustment.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2060324\" style=\"width: 360px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2060324\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2060324\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg\" alt=\"An iPhone showing the camera app shooting in RAW mode.\" width=\"350\" height=\"709\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg 426w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg?resize=74,150 74w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg?resize=148,300 148w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg?resize=336,680 336w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple_proraw.jpg?resize=25,50 25w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 350px) 100vw, 350px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2060324\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>RAW files are the answer to this, as DSLR photographers know â€” they&#8217;re a minimally processed representation of what the sensor collects, letting the user do all the work to make the photo look good. Being able to shoot to a RAW format (or RAW-adjacent; we&#8217;ll know more with hands-on testing) frees up photographers who may have felt hemmed in by the iPhone&#8217;s default image processing. There were ways of getting around this before, but Apple has an advantage over third-party apps with its low-level access to the camera architecture, so this format will probably be the new standard.</p>\n<p>This newfound elasticity at the image format level also enables the iPhone Pros to shoot in Dolby Vision, a grading standard usually applied in editing suites after you shoot your movie or commercial on a digital cinema camera. Shooting directly to it may be helpful to people planning to use the format but shooting with iPhones as B cameras. If cinematographer Emmanuel Lubezki approves, it&#8217;s good enough for pretty much everyone else on Earth. I sincerely doubt anyone will cut their work together on the phone, though.</p>\n<p>These two advances, ProRAW and Dolby, suggest that Apple&#8217;s improved silicon has left a lot of wiggle room in the photography backend. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/22/the-future-of-photography-is-code/\">As I&#8217;ve written before,</a> this is the most important segment of the imaging workflow right now, and the company is probably coming up with all kinds of ways to take advantage of the power offered by the latest chips.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"jYOhmXq12Z\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/22/the-future-of-photography-is-code/\">The future of photography is code</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;The future of photography is code&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/22/the-future-of-photography-is-code/embed/#?secret=jYOhmXq12Z\" data-secret=\"jYOhmXq12Z\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Though larger cameras and lenses still offer advantages that the iPhone can never hope to match, the reverse is true as well. And the closer the iPhone gets to offering cinema-like quality â€” even if it&#8217;s simulated â€” the greater its advantages of portability and ease of use grow in proportion. Apple has been ruthlessly targeting enthusiast photographers, who aren&#8217;t quite sure if they want to buy a DSLR or mirrorless system in addition to a phone with a nice camera. By sweetening the deal on the phone side, Apple surely rakes in more of these users every generation.</p>\n<p>Of course the Pro phones come at a significant premium over the normal range of iPhone devices (the Max <em>starts</em> at $1,099), but these improvements aren&#8217;t impossible or really even difficult to bring to lower-end models â€” most of them will probably trickle down next year. Of course, by then a whole new set of features will have been cooked up for the Pro devices. For photographers, however, planned obsolescence is part of the lifestyle.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/apple-iphone-event-2020\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/apple-iphone-event-2020.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=HQgnC_KXgc4:_qavXZNNWiE:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a
